figma: https://www.figma.com/design/oKCEM0ZarKowNcQEnxnwud/Tech-Interview-_-Frontend-engineer?node-id=0-1&t=Do6EcrKkrgIBZCvS-1

# Production-Ready CMS and Frontend Integration: A Step-by-Step Implementation Guide

This reference document outlines the blueprint and methodology for designing, developing, and deploying a production-ready Content Management System (CMS) integrated with a dynamic, public-facing web application. This guide is crafted to help beginners build clean, secure, and highly scalable software solutions.

## 1. Objective

The primary objective of this project is to replace static, hardcoded frontend elements with a fully dynamic, database-driven architecture managed through an authenticated Admin Dashboard.

By separating the **Admin Management System (CMS)** from the **Public Frontend Layout**, you will build a decoupled headless architecture where content is managed flexibly.

The application must handle complex, rich structured text including:

- Nested lists and complex text hierarchies.
- Structured data tables.
- Inline and block mathematical notation parsed using LaTeX syntax
- Structured technical documentation.

## 2. Technical Requirements

Before beginning, ensure your system has the following requirements installed:

### A. Environment & Runtimes

- **Node.js**: Version `v18.x` or `v20.x` (LTS is recommended)
- **Package Manager**: `npm` (packaged with Node) or `yarn` / `pnpm`
- **Docker Engine & Desktop**: Needed to containerize resources (database and applications)

### B. Suggested Stack

- **Database**: MongoDB (via `mongoose`) or PostgreSQL (via `prisma`)
- **Backend**: Express.js with Node, secure password hashing (`bcryptjs`), and token session state (`jsonwebtoken`)
- **Admin Frontend**: React.js, Optional (Redux Toolkit (state management)), and Tailwind CSS (styling)
- **Public Frontend**: React.js (or Next.js) for layout rendering, Tailwind CSS, and KaTeX (for mathematical equations)
- **Rich Text Support**: TipTap, Editor.js, or Draft.js for standard block operations

## 3. Step-by-Step Instructions

This sequential checklist breaks down development into manageable, testable milestones.

### Step 1: Design the Content Model (Data Strategy)

Because content types on a website range from simple strings to nested list structures, tables, and mathematical formulas, a flat database schema will not scale. You must represent content in "Blocks."

1. Identify the layouts required by the Figma design (Hero, Grid, Text Section, Formulas, Table).
2. Establish a **Block-Based Schema** design. A page contains an array of "Content Blocks". Each block has a `type` (e.g., `"header"`, `"text"`, `"table"`, `"math"`) and a variable `data` field holding schema-conforming elements.

### Step 2: Establish the Development Environment (Monorepo)

For local development, bundle both frontends and the backend in a unified structure for simplicity.

1. Create a root project folder.
2. Structure the directory into three logical subdirectories: `/backend`, `/admin-frontend`, and `/public-frontend`.
3. Configure your local `.env` files matching key variables like database connection strings, JWT secret tokens, and server ports.

### Step 3: Implement the Express Backend

1. Initialize the backend workspace with `npm init -y` and install essential dependencies (`express`, `mongoose`, `cors`, `dotenv`, `jsonwebtoken`, `bcryptjs`).
2. Construct a basic Express server and connect it to your database.
3. Establish robust central routing handlers for `/api/v1/auth` and `/api/v1/content`.
4. Apply global error-handling middlewares and schema validation (using libraries like `zod` or custom Express middleware) to avoid malformed payloads.

### Step 4: Secure the API via Authentication

1. Define an admin user schema with fields for username, email, and password. Store passwords securely with `bcryptjs` hashing.
2. Build an authentication route `/api/v1/auth/login`. Verify user credentials and sign a JSON Web Token (JWT) containing administrative claims.
3. Build a JWT validation middleware to intercept incoming requests on administrative endpoints. If the verification fails, block access with a `401 Unauthorized` or `403 Forbidden` status.

### Step 5: Construct the Admin Panel Dashboard

1. Set up a boilerplate React application in `/admin-frontend` using Vite.
2. Implement Redux Toolkit to act as your global state container. Configure a slice for authentication (`authSlice.js`) to cache the active admin session and JWT token.
3. Build secure routes inside your router config (using `react-router-dom`). Unauthenticated requests should instantly redirect to a clean LoginPage.
4. Set up an Admin Panel layout with dynamic sidebar navigation, providing clean options to create, edit, update, or list dynamic pages.

### Step 6: Integrate the Block-Based Editor

1. Choose a structured content editor (TipTap or Editor.js are highly recommended as they export content clean, nested JSON blocks rather than messy raw HTML).
2. Build validation inputs for tables, lists, or custom math inputs where the editor can safely insert formulas formatted with raw LaTeX syntax (e.g., wrapping statements with `$` tags).
3. Connect the edit form actions to Redux Toolkit dispatch actions to persist structural state adjustments back to your Express server.

### Step 7: Build the Public Frontend layout

1. Set up a separate lightweight React instance in `/public-frontend`.
2. Map endpoints of your backend to the public consumer routes.
3. Since content block output can be complex, build a layout parser component (`BlockRenderer.jsx`). This element will switch rendering logic depending on block types (e.g., rendering markdown text, displaying lists dynamically, constructing table rows, or typesetting math formulas using a specialized renderer like `react-katex`).
4. Apply the Figma design styles using custom Tailwind classes to make the visual representation polished and responsive.

### Step 8: Dockerize the Environment

1. Write a `Dockerfile` for each separate codebase (backend, admin, and public).
2. Configure a root `docker-compose.yml` to spin up a localized database instance, start your Express app, and mount both the admin and public web services under a unified network interface.

## 4. Project Structure

```
cms-assignment/
├── docker-compose.yml
├── README.md
├── .env.example
│
├── backend/
│   ├── src/
│   │   ├── config/          # Database, Authentication, environment configs
│   │   ├── controllers/     # Authentication & Content business logic handlers
│   │   ├── middleware/      # JWT guards, validation check pipelines
│   │   ├── models/          # Database structural schemas (Mongoose)
│   │   ├── routes/          # Express route definitions
│   │   └── server.js        # Server launch file
│   ├── package.json
│   └── Dockerfile
│
├── admin-frontend/
│   ├── src/
│   │   ├── components/      # UI buttons, Admin shell layouts, Editor components
│   │   ├── pages/           # Admin Login, Pages Dashboard, Page Builder view
│   │   ├── store/           # Redux Toolkit store config, Auth slice, Pages slice
│   │   ├── utils/           # Helper scripts and HTTP instance interceptors
│   │   └── App.jsx
│   ├── package.json
│   └── Dockerfile
│
└── public-frontend/
    ├── src/
    │   ├── components/      # Common navigation wrappers, dynamic BlockRenderer
    │   ├── pages/           # Catch-all landing page, Article layouts
    │   ├── utils/           # Data fetch mechanisms
    │   └── App.jsx
    ├── package.json
    └── Dockerfile
```

## 5. Key Example Snippets

### A. Database Model (`backend/src/models/Page.js`)

This mongoose schema shows how to handle block structures. Instead of unstructured HTML, we use a structured content block array.

```
const mongoose = require('mongoose');

// Schema representing block-level modular items
const BlockSchema = new mongoose.Schema({
  type: {
    type: String,
    enum: ['header', 'paragraph', 'list', 'table', 'equation'],
    required: true
  },
  // We utilize "Mixed" because the data format varies with each block type
  data: {
    type: mongoose.Schema.Types.Mixed,
    required: true
  },
  order: {
    type: Number,
    required: true,
    default: 0
  }
});

const PageSchema = new mongoose.Schema({
  title: {
    type: String,
    required: [true, 'A page title is required'],
    trim: true
  },
  slug: {
    type: String,
    required: true,
    unique: true,
    lowercase: true,
    trim: true
  },
  blocks: [BlockSchema]
}, {
  timestamps: true
});

module.exports = mongoose.model('Page', PageSchema);
```

### B. Express JWT Gate Middleware (`backend/src/middleware/authMiddleware.js`)

Validates administrator access rights before allowing content adjustments.

```
const jwt = require('jsonwebtoken');

const protectRoute = (req, res, next) => {
  let token;

  // Retrieve token from Authorization header (Format: Bearer <token>)
  if (req.headers.authorization && req.headers.authorization.startsWith('Bearer')) {
    token = req.headers.authorization.split(' ')[1];
  }

  if (!token) {
    return res.status(401).json({
      success: false,
      message: 'Access denied. No authentication credentials found.'
    });
  }

  try {
    const decoded = jwt.verify(token, process.env.JWT_SECRET || 'fallback_secret');
    req.admin = { id: decoded.id, username: decoded.username };
    next();
  } catch (error) {
    return res.status(403).json({
      success: false,
      message: 'Invalid or expired authorization token.'
    });
  }
};

module.exports = protectRoute;
```

### C. Redux Auth Slice (`admin-frontend/src/store/slices/authSlice.js`)

Manages authentication token lifetimes, authentication status, and API requests cleanly.

```
import { createSlice, createAsyncThunk } from '@reduxjs/toolkit';

// Assume API calls use a configuration class with custom interceptors
import api from '../../utils/api';

export const loginAdmin = createAsyncThunk(
  'auth/loginAdmin',
  async (credentials, { rejectWithValue }) => {
    try {
      const response = await api.post('/auth/login', credentials);
      localStorage.setItem('adminToken', response.data.token);
      return response.data;
    } catch (err) {
      return rejectWithValue(err.response?.data?.message || 'Login failed');
    }
  }
);

const authSlice = createSlice({
  name: 'auth',
  initialState: {
    token: localStorage.getItem('adminToken') || null,
    isAuthenticated: !!localStorage.getItem('adminToken'),
    isLoading: false,
    error: null
  },
  reducers: {
    logout: (state) => {
      localStorage.removeItem('adminToken');
      state.token = null;
      state.isAuthenticated = false;
      state.error = null;
    }
  },
  extraReducers: (builder) => {
    builder
      .addCase(loginAdmin.pending, (state) => {
        state.isLoading = true;
        state.error = null;
      })
      .addCase(loginAdmin.fulfilled, (state, action) => {
        state.isLoading = false;
        state.isAuthenticated = true;
        state.token = action.payload.token;
      })
      .addCase(loginAdmin.rejected, (state, action) => {
        state.isLoading = false;
        state.error = action.payload;
      });
  }
});

export const { logout } = authSlice.actions;
export default authSlice.reducer;
```

### D. Mathematical and Complex Block Parser (`public-frontend/src/components/BlockRenderer.jsx`)

Parses nested object arrays and cleanly renders elements including LaTeX mathematical expressions.

```
import React from 'react';
import 'katex/dist/katex.min.css';
import { InlineMath, BlockMath } from 'react-katex';

const BlockRenderer = ({ blocks = [] }) => {
  // Sort blocks based on structural database sequence order
  const sortedBlocks = [...blocks].sort((a, b) => a.order - b.order);

  return (
    <div className="space-y-6">
      {sortedBlocks.map((block) => {
        switch (block.type) {
          case 'header':
            return (
              <h2 key={block._id} className="text-3xl font-bold tracking-tight text-gray-900">
                {block.data.text}
              </h2>
            );

          case 'paragraph':
            return (
              <p key={block._id} className="text-base leading-7 text-gray-700">
                {block.data.text}
              </p>
            );

          case 'list':
            return (
              <ul key={block._id} className="list-disc pl-6 space-y-2 text-gray-700">
                {block.data.items.map((item, index) => (
                  <li key={index}>{item}</li>
                ))}
              </ul>
            );

          case 'equation':
            const { equation, displayMode } = block.data;
            return (
              <div key={block._id} className="my-4 p-4 bg-gray-50 rounded-lg overflow-x-auto">
                {displayMode ? (
                  <BlockMath math={equation} />
                ) : (
                  <p className="flex items-center gap-2">
                    <span className="text-sm text-gray-500 font-mono">[Formula]:</span>
                    <InlineMath math={equation} />
                  </p>
                )}
              </div>
            );

          case 'table':
            const { headers, rows } = block.data;
            return (
              <div key={block._id} className="overflow-x-auto my-6 border border-gray-200 rounded-lg">
                <table className="min-w-full divide-y divide-gray-200">
                  <thead className="bg-gray-50">
                    <tr>
                      {headers.map((header, idx) => (
                        <th key={idx} className="px-6 py-3 text-left text-xs font-semibold uppercase tracking-wider text-gray-500">
                          {header}
                        </th>
                      ))}
                    </tr>
                  </thead>
                  <tbody className="divide-y divide-gray-200 bg-white">
                    {rows.map((row, rIdx) => (
                      <tr key={rIdx}>
                        {row.map((cell, cIdx) => (
                          <td key={cIdx} className="whitespace-nowrap px-6 py-4 text-sm text-gray-700">
                            {cell}
                          </td>
                        ))}
                      </tr>
                    ))}
                  </tbody>
                </table>
              </div>
            );

          default:
            return (
              <div key={block._id} className="p-3 bg-yellow-50 text-yellow-800 text-xs rounded border">
                Unknown content block format: {block.type}
              </div>
            );
        }
      })}
    </div>
  );
};

export default BlockRenderer;
